Res. 17, 689â704 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1261">50</a></sup> with important anti-influenza, anti-inflammatory, and leukocyte inhibition effects<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Chang, S. J., Chang, Y. C., Lu, K. Z., Tsou, Y. Y. &amp; Lin, C. W. Antiviral activity of Isatis indigotica extract and its derived indirubin against Japanese encephalitis virus. Evid. Based Complement Alternat. Med. 2012, 925830 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1266">11</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Hoessel, R. et al. Indirubin, the active constituent of a Chinese antileukaemia medicine, inhibits cyclin-dependent kinases. Nat. Cell Biol. 1, 60â67 (1999)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1269">23</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Mak, N. K. et al. Inhibition of RANTES expression by indirubin in influenza virus-infected human bronchial epithelial cells. Biochem. Pharmacol. 67, 167â174 (2004)." href="#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1272">51</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Kunikata, T. et al. Indirubin inhibits inflammatory reactions in delayed-type hypersensitivity. Eur. J. Pharmacol. 410, 93â100 (2000)." href="#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1272_1">52</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Salvini, M. et al. Alpha-tryptophan synthase of Isatis tinctoria: gene cloning and expression. Plant Physiol. Biochem. 46, 715â723 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1275">53</a></sup>. Based on the KEGG maps and previously suggested pathways<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Chen, J. et al. Biosynthesis of the active compounds of Isatis indigotica based on transcriptome sequencing and metabolites profiling. BMC Genomics 14, 857â857 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1279">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Hsu, T. M. et al. Employing a biochemical protecting group for a sustainable indigo dyeing strategy. Nat. Chem. Biol. 14, 256 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1282">54</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Sheng, H. et al. Altering regioselectivity cytochrome P450 BM-3 saturation mutagenes is for the biosynthesis of indirubin. J. Mol. Catal. B 67, 29â35 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1285">55</a></sup>, we identified 32 genes that encoded 11 enzymes involved in the biosynthesis of indole alkaloids (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#Fig3">3c</a> and Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#MOESM1">S16</a>). Because of the lack of downstream pathways, other genes for indole alkaloid biosynthesis in <i>I. indigotica</i> need further identification. It should be noted that numerous genes involved in the biosynthesis of the three major types of active compounds increased in copy number because of tandem duplication, for example, geranylgeranyl diphosphate synthase, cinnamate 4-hydroxylase, 4-coumarate-CoA ligase, and indole-3-pyruvate monooxygenase (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#Fig3">3</a> and Supplementary Tables <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#MOESM1">S14</a>â<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#MOESM1">S16</a>).</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec8" data-title="Discussion"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec8-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec8">Discussion</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec8-content"><p>Continuity and completeness are important indicators of genome assembly. PacBio-based genome assembly plus error corrections based on Illumina data could greatly improve continuity and completeness<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Korlach, J. et al. De novo PacBio long-read and phased avian genome assemblies correct and add to reference genes generated with intermediate and short reads. GigaScience 6, gix085 (2017)." href="#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1317">56</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhang, L. et al. Improved Brassica rapa reference genome by single-molecule sequencing and chromosome conformation capture technologies. Horticult. Res. 5, 50 (2018)." href="#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1317_1">57</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Chen, J. et al. Liriodendron genome sheds light on angiosperm phylogeny and speciesâpair differentiation. Nat. Plants 5, 18 (2019)." href="#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1317_2">58</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Hu, Y. et al. Gossypium barbadense and Gossypium hirsutum genomes provide insights into the origin and evolution of allotetraploid cotton. Nat. Genet. 51, 739â748 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1320">59</a></sup>. Our genome assembly of <i>I. indigotica</i> by this strategy showed a highly resolved result with an N50â=â1.22âMb and longest contig lengthâ=â8.99âMb. In addition, we used Hi-C data to cluster the contigs into seven pseudochromosomes with a final scaffold N50â=â36.17âMb and longest chromosome lengthâ=â38.25âMb. The completeness and high quality of the present <i>I. indigotica</i> genome were further confirmed by BUSCO and comparative chromosome analyses<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Lysak, M. A., MandÃ¡kovÃ¡, T. &amp; Schranz, M. E. Comparative paleogenomics of crucifers: ancestral genomic blocks revisited. Curr. Opin. Plant Biol. 30, 108â115 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1330">32</a></sup>. A total of 97.22% of the genes examined by BUSCO were complete, and the chromosome structure of <i>I. indigotica</i> was consistent with the tPCK type.</p><p>We constructed the phylogenetic relationships of <i>I. indigotica</i> based on genomic data and found that <i>I. indigotica</i> of Isatideae is sister to <i>S. irio</i> of Sisymbrieae among the sampled species, consistent with the results of previously published phylogenetic analyses<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Al-Shehbaz, I., Beilstein, M. A. &amp; Kellogg, E. Systematics and phylogeny of the Brassicaceae (Cruciferae): an overview. Plant Syst. Evol. 259, 89â120 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1349">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Beilstein, M., Al-Shehbaz, I. &amp; Kellogg, E. Brassicaceae phylogeny and trichome evolution. Am. J. Bot. 93, 607â619 (2006)." href="#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1352">6</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Beilstein, M. A., Al-Shehbaz, I. A., Sarah, M. &amp; Kellogg, E. A. Brassicaceae phylogeny inferred from phytochrome A and ndhF sequence data: tribes and trichomes revisited. Am. J. Bot. 95, 1307â1327 (2008)." href="#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1352_1">7</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Franzke, A., Lysak, M. A., Al-Shehbaz, I. A., Koch, M. A. &amp; Mummenhoff, K. Cabbage family affairs: the evolutionary history of Brassicaceae. Trends Plant Sci. 16, 108â116 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1355">8</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Nikolov, L. A. et al. Resolving the backbone of the Brassicaceae phylogeny for investigating trait diversity. N. Phytol. 222, 1638â1651 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1358">10</a></sup>. Based on the phylogenetic results, we identified expanded and contracted gene families in <i>I. indigotica</i>. The expanded genes in this species were mainly derived from tandem duplications and were obviously enriched in some secondary metabolite pathways. Based on homolog searching and functional annotation in our high-quality genome, we further identified candidate genes for the biosynthesis of three main classes of active compounds in <i>I. indigotica</i>: terpenoids, phenylpropanoids, and indole alkaloids. These candidate genes complete or replenish gene sets for biosynthetic pathways of these compounds concentrated in <i>I. indigotica</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Chen, J. et al. Biosynthesis of the active compounds of Isatis indigotica based on transcriptome sequencing and metabolites profiling. BMC Genomics 14, 857â857 (2013)." href="#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1371">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Gai, Q. Y. et al. Elicitation of Isatis tinctoria L. hairy root cultures by salicylic acid and methyl jasmonate for the enhanced production of pharmacologically active alkaloids and flavonoids. Plant Cell 137, 77â86 (2019)." href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1371_1">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Lu, B. B. et al. Cloning and characterization of a differentially expressed phenylalanine ammonialyase gene (IiPAL) after genome duplication from tetraploid Isatis indigotica Fort. J. Integr. Plant Biol. 48, 1439â1449 (2006)." href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1371_2">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Hu, Y. et al. Isolation and characterization of a gene encoding cinnamoyl-CoA reductase from Isatis indigotica Fort. Mol. Biol. Rep. 38, 2075â2083 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1374">28</a></sup> (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#Fig3">3</a>). In addition, we found that in some synthesis steps, the copy number of enzyme-coding genes increased to two or more because of tandem duplications. The increase in copy number may drive the production of major active compounds in <i>I. indigotica</i> and account for its excellent antibacterial and antiviral activities because gene expansions are responsible for enhancing a special trait or the origin of a new trait<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Chae, L., Kim, T., Nilo-Poyanco, R. &amp; Rhee, S. Y. Genomic signatures of specialized metabolism in plants. Science 344, 510â513 (2014)." href="#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1384">60</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Kliebenstein, D. J. A role for gene duplication and natural variation of gene expression in the evolution of metabolism. PLoS ONE 3, e1838 (2008)." href="#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1384_1">61</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Kliebenstein, D. J., Lambrix, V. M., Reichelt, M., Gershenzon, J. &amp; Mitchell-Olds, T. Gene duplication in the diversification of secondary metabolism: tandem 2-oxoglutarate-dependent dioxygenases control glucosinolate biosynthesis in Arabidopsis. Plant Cell 13, 681â693 (2001)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1387">62</a></sup>.</p><p>Overall, in this study, we present a high-quality genome for <i>I. indigotica</i>. We further identify or replenish candidate genes for biosynthesis pathways of the active compounds in this medicinal plant. These genes and genomic resources will provide a solid basis for future biosynthesis-related studies.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec9" data-title="Materials and methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec9-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec9">Materials and methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec9-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10">DNA extraction and genome sequencing</h3><p>We initially extracted high-quality total DNA from fresh young leaves of a 2-month-old plant artificially cultivated in the greenhouse using the cetyltrimethylammonium bromide method. We used a SMRTbell Template Prep Kit 1.0 (PacBio, Menlo Park, CA, USA) to construct the DNA libraries for PacBio long-read sequencing and sequenced them on a PacBio Sequel system. We obtained a total of four SMRT cells with 39.94âGb of sequencing data (coverage of 142.71Ã) from the PacBio Sequel platform and generated a total of 4.30 million subreads with an N50 read length of 14.9âkb (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#MOESM1">S1</a> and Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#MOESM1">S1</a>). We also prepared paired-end Illumina libraries using an Illumina Genomic DNA Sample Preparation Kit and sequenced them on an Illumina HiSeq X Ten system for error correction and K-mer analysis and generated a total of 37.50âGb of data and 31.79âGb of clean data (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#MOESM1">S1</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec11">Genome assembly and pseudochromosome construction</h3><p>We initially estimated the genome size of <i>I. indigotica</i> by flow cytometry with <i>Vigna radiata</i> as the reference<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Kang, Y. J. et al. Genome sequence of mungbean and insights into evolution within Vigna species. Nat. Commun. 5, 5443 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1432">63</a></sup>. We then used clean Illumina short reads to calculate K-mers (Illumina DNA short read size of 19âbp) by Jellyfish v.2.2.9<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="MarÃ§ais, G. &amp; Kingsford, C. A fast, lock-free approach for efficient parallel counting of occurrences of k-mers. Bioinformatics 27, 764 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1436">64</a></sup> to confirm the genome size. The sequencing depth was estimated by determining the highest peak value of the frequency curve of the K-mer occurrence distribution. We used SMRT Link pipeline v.5.1.0.26412 to process the polymerase reads into subreads with readScoreâ=â0.75 and minSubReadLengthâ=â500 and used Canu v.1.6<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Koren, S. et al. Canu: scalable and accurate long-read assembly via adaptive k-mer weighting and repeat separation. Genome Res. 27, 722 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1440">65</a></sup> to correct errors of the PacBio subreads and assemble the corrected reads into contigs after trimming low-quality bases using WTDBG (<a href="https://github.com/ruanjue/wtdbg">https://github.com/ruanjue/wtdbg</a>). We corrected the assembled contigs by using 270âbp PE Illumina data by Pilon v.1.13<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Walker, B. J. et al. Pilon: an integrated tool for comprehensive microbial variant detection and genome assembly improvement. PLoS ONE 9, e112963 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1449">66</a></sup> and finally obtained a 293.83âMb contig-scale assembly with a contig N50 of 1.22âMb. The genome contained 1162 contigs, and the longest contig was 8.99âMb with a 38.18% GC content. These contigs were further anchored to chromosomes by the Hi-C technique.</p><p>We grounded ~3âg of fresh young leaf tissue into powder in liquid nitrogen for Hi-C experiments and constructed a Hi-C library following Louwers et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Louwers, M., Splinter, E., Driel, R. V., Laat, W. D. &amp; Stam, M. Studying physical chromatin interactions in plants using Chromosome Conformation Capture (3C). Nat. Protoc. 4, 1216â1229 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1456">67</a></sup> with chromatin extraction and digestion and DNA ligation, purification, and fragmentation. Finally, we obtained a total of 79.43âGb of clean reads for Hi-C analyses by the Illumina HiSeq X Ten platform. We first carried out a preliminary assembly by splitting contigs into segments of 100âkb on average and mapping the Hi-C data to the contigs using BWA v.0.7.10-r789<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with BurrowsâWheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754â1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1460">68</a></sup> in order to correct contig errors. We then used LACHESIS software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Burton, J. N. et al. Chromosome-scale scaffolding of de novo genome assemblies based on chromatin interactions. Nat. Biotechnol. 31, 1119 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1464">69</a></sup> with the parameters CLUSTER MIN RE SITESâ=â22, CLUSTER MAX LINK DENSITYâ=â2, CLUSTER NONINFORMATIVE RATIOâ=â2, ORDER MIN N RES IN TRUNâ=â10, and ORDER MIN N RES IN SHREDSâ=â10 to cluster and reorder all corrected contigs into pseudochromosomes. We finally adjusted the order and direction of the contigs on the pseudochromosomes by examining their interactions in the Hi-C heatmap. We evaluated the completeness and quality of the final assembled genome through BUSCO v.3.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="SimÃ£O, F. A., Waterhouse, R. M., Panagiotis, I., Kriventseva, E. V. &amp; Zdobnov, E. M. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics 31, 3210â3212 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1468">29</a></sup> tests using gene content from the Embryophyta_odb9 database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="SimÃ£O, F. A., Waterhouse, R. M., Panagiotis, I., Kriventseva, E. V. &amp; Zdobnov, E. M. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics 31, 3210â3212 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1472">29</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec12">Repeat annotation</h3><p>We identified repetitive elements through both RepeatModeler v.1.0.10 and RepeatMasker v.4.0.7<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Chen, N. Using RepeatMasker to identify repetitive elements in genomic sequences. Curr. Protoc. Bioinformatics 5, 4â10 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1484">70</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Price, A. L., Jones, N. C. &amp; Pevzner, P. A. De novo identification of repeat families in large genomes. Bioinformatics 21(Suppl. 1), i351 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1487">71</a></sup>. RepeatModeler employed RECON and RepeatScout to predict interspersed repeats and then obtained the consensus repeat library. RepeatMasker recovered the repeats in the <i>I. indigotica</i> genome through a homology-based repeat search using the ab initio repeat database and Repbase. The overlapping repeats belonging to the same repeat class were combined according to their coordination in the genome. The overlapping repeats belonging to different repeat classes were then split into different types.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec13">Gene prediction and functional annotation</h3><p>To improve gene prediction, we further obtained transcriptomes by sequencing high-quality RNA from mixed fresh leaf, flower, and stem tissues and sequenced them by the Illumina HiSeq X Ten platform. We removed adapters and discarded reads with &gt;10% N bases or reads having more than 20% bases of low quality (below 5) using NGS QC Toolkit v.2.3.3<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Patel, R. K. &amp; Mukesh, J. NGS QC Toolkit: a toolkit for quality control of next generation sequencing data. PLos ONE 7, e30619 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1502">72</a></sup> and finally generated 19.87âGb of clean data. We assembled the de novo and genome-guided transcriptomes with clean reads by Trinity v.2.4.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Grabherr, M. G. et al. Trinity: reconstructing a full-length transcriptome without a genome from RNA-seq data. Nat. Biotechnol. 29, 644â652 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1506">73</a></sup>. We also mapped the RNA-sequencing (RNA-seq) reads to the assembled genome to obtain the mapping rate through HISAT2 v.2.1.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Daehwan, K., Ben, L. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. HISAT: a fast spliced aligner with low memory requirements. Nat. Methods 12, 357â360 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1510">74</a></sup> to evaluate the completeness of the genome.</p><p>We run PASA pipeline v.2.1.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using EVidenceModeler and the program to assemble spliced alignments. Genome Biol. 9, R7 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1517">75</a></sup> to align the transcripts to the assembled genome to carry out ORF prediction and gene prediction. To train the HMM model for Augustus, we extracted complete, multiexon genes, removed redundant high-identity genes (cut-off all-to-all identity of 70%), and finally generated the best candidate and low-identity gene models for training. We aligned the RNA-seq data to the hard-masked genome assembly by HISAT2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Daehwan, K., Ben, L. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. HISAT: a fast spliced aligner with low memory requirements. Nat. Methods 12, 357â360 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1521">74</a></sup> and used bam2hints in Augustus to generate the intron hint file. We used this hint file to carry out ab initio gene prediction by Augustus v.3.2.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Mario, S., Rasmus, S., Stephan, W. &amp; Burkhard, M. AUGUSTUS: a web server for gene finding in eukaryotes. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 309â312 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1525">76</a></sup>. For homologous prediction, the reference protein sequences of <i>Brassica rapa</i>, <i>Brassica napus</i>, <i>Raphanus sativus</i>, <i>Brassica juncea</i>, and <i>Brassica nigra</i> were downloaded and aligned against the <i>I. indigotica</i> genome using TBLASTN v.2.2.31<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 421 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1548">77</a></sup> and searched with an <i>e</i> value of 1e<sup>â5</sup>. After filtering low-quality results, gene structure was predicted using GeneWise v.2.4.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Birney, E., Clamp, M. &amp; Durbin, R. GeneWise and genomewise. Genome Res. 14, 988â995 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1558">78</a></sup>. We combined the results from PASA, Augustus and GeneWise to generate the final protein-coding gene set using EVidenceModeler v.1.1.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using EVidenceModeler and the program to assemble spliced alignments. Genome Biol. 9, R7 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1562">75</a></sup>. To obtain the untranslated regions and alternatively spliced isoforms, we used PASA to update the gff3 file for two rounds and obtain the final gene models.</p><p>We annotated the functions of the predicated genes against public databases by NCBI BLAST+ v.2.2.31<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 421 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1569">77</a></sup> with a cut-off <i>e</i> value of 1e<sup>â5</sup> and maximum number of target sequences of 20, including the Swiss-Prot and TrEMBL databases<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Bairoch, A. &amp; Apweiler, R. The SWISS-PROT protein sequence database and its supplement TrEMBL in 2000. Nucleic Acids Res. 28, 45â48 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1578">79</a></sup>. Best-hit BLAST results were then used to define gene functions. We used InterProScan v.5.25-64.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Zdobnov, E. M. &amp; Apweiler, R. InterProScanâan integration platform for the signature-recognition methods in InterPro. Bioinformatics 17, 847â848 (2001)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1582">80</a></sup> to identify motifs and domains by matching against public databases. We identified GO annotations by using Blast2GO v.4.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Conesa, A. &amp; GÃ¶tz, S. Blast2GO: a comprehensive suite for functional analysis in plant genomics. Int. J. Plant Genomics 2008, 619832 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1587">81</a></sup> according to the blast results and combined them with InterPro GO entries. We mapped the existing GO terms to enzyme codes by Blast2GO and submitted the predicted proteins to the KEGG (Kyoto Encyclopedia of Genes and Genomes) Automatic Annotation Server (KAAS)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Moriya, Y., Itoh, M., Okuda, S., Yoshizawa, A. C. &amp; Kanehisa, M. KAAS: an automatic genome annotation and pathway reconstruction server. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, W182âW185 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1591">82</a></sup> to obtain KO numbers for KEGG pathway annotation.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec14">Gene family and phylogenetic analyses</h3><p>We used protein sequences of <i>I. indigotica</i> and eight other Brassicaceae species (<i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i>, <i>Capsella rubella</i>, <i>Brassica rapa</i>, <i>Brassica napus</i>, <i>Raphanus sativus</i>, <i>Schrenkiella parvula</i>, <i>Sisymbrium irio</i>, and <i>Eutrema salsugineum</i>) with the outgroup species <i>Cleome hassleriana</i> for same-family gene clustering. For genes with alternative splicing variants, the longest transcript was selected to represent the gene. Similarities between sequence pairs were calculated using BLASTP v.2.2.31<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 421 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1635">77</a></sup> with a cut-off <i>e</i> value of 1e<sup>â5</sup>. Additionally, OrthoMCL v.2.0.9 was used with default parameters to assess gene family membership based on overall gene similarity combined with Markov Chain Clustering (MCL) v.14-137<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C. J. &amp; Roos, D. S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178â2189 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1645">83</a></sup>.</p><p>We extracted single-copy orthologous genes from the ten species by OrthoMCL and aligned the resulting protein sequences by MAFFT v.7.313<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Katoh, K. &amp; Standley, D. M. MAFFT multiple sequence alignment software version 7: improvements in performance and usability. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 772â780 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1652">84</a></sup>. Then, we used Gblocks v.0.91b<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 85" title="Castresana, J. Selection of conserved blocks from multiple alignments for their use in phylogenetic analysis. Mol. Biol. Evol. 17, 540â552 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR85" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1656">85</a></sup> to extract the conserved sites of multiple sequence alignments and constructed a phylogenetic tree by RAxML v.8.2.11<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 86" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML version 8: a tool for phylogenetic analysis and post-analysis of large phylogenies. Bioinformatics 30, 1312â1313 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1660">86</a></sup>. We used <i>C. hassleriana</i> as an outgroup and performed 1000 bootstrap analyses to test the robustness of each branch. We used the Bayesian relaxed molecular clock approach in MCMCTREE of PAML v.4.9e<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 87" title="Yang, Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586â1591 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1667">87</a></sup> to estimate divergence time. We calibrated this tree based on the estimated divergence times in the TimeTree database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 88" title="Kumar, S., Stecher, G., Suleski, M. &amp; Hedges, S. B. TimeTree: a resource for timelines, timetrees, and divergence times. Mol. Biol. Evol. 34, 1812â1819 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR88" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1672">88</a></sup> for <i>C. hassleriana</i>â<i>A. thaliana</i> (35â59âMya), <i>A. thaliana</i>â<i>C. rubella</i> (7.4â12.8âMya), <i>B. rapaâS. parvula</i> (19.3â28.6âMya), and <i>B. rapaâA. thaliana</i> (23.4â33.5âMya).</p><p>Gene families that had undergone expansion or contraction were identified in the eight sequenced species using CAFE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 89" title="Han, M. V., Thomas, G. W. C., Jose, L. M. &amp; Hahn, M. W. Estimating gene gain and loss rates in the presence of error in genome assembly and annotation using CAFE 3. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 1987â1997 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR89" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1698">89</a></sup>. The CAFE parameters included a <i>p</i> value thresholdâ=â0.05 and automatic searching for the <i>Î»</i> value. The algorithm in CAFE takes a matrix of gene family sizes in extant species as input and uses a probabilistic graphical model to ascertain the rate and direction of changes in gene family size across a given phylogenetic tree.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec15">WGD analysis and identification of tandemly repeated genes</h3><p>To examine WGD in <i>I. indigotica</i> and <i>B. rapa</i>, we extracted all homologous proteins between these two species and <i>A. thaliana</i> using an all-to-all search in BLASTP v.2.2.31<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 421 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1725">77</a></sup> with an <i>e</i> value cut-off of 1e<sup>â9</sup>. We used MCScanX<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 90" title="Wang, Y. et al. MCScanX: a toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, e49âe49 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR90" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1735">90</a></sup> with default parameters to identify collinear blocks, each containing at least five collinear gene pairs. To infer WGD events, we used the downstream MCScanX script add_ka_and_ks_to_collinearity.pl to calculate the Ks values between collinear genes among these three genomes. We further performed whole-genome alignment of the three species by LAST v.946<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 91" title="KieÅbasa, S. M., Wan, R., Sato, K., Horton, P. &amp; Frith, M. C. Adaptive seeds tame genomic sequence comparison. Genome Res. 21, 487â493 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR91" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1739">91</a></sup> and constructed a dot plot by the downstream program last-dotplot.</p><p>Identification of tandem repeat genes in the <i>I. indigotica</i> genome was based on three criteria: (1) two or more genes had more than 70% identity and 70% coverage according to BLASTP; (2) the pairwise gene distance was &lt;100âkb; and (3) there were no more than 10 genes lying between the repeat genes on a single scaffold<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 92" title="Hanada, K., Zou, C., Lehti-Shiu, M. D., Shinozaki, K. &amp; Shiu, S. H. Importance of lineage-specific expansion of plant tandem duplicates in the adaptive response to environmental stimuli. Plant Physiol. 148, 993â1003 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0240-5#ref-CR92" id="ref-link-section-d40061e1749">92</a></sup>. The genes identified in this way were subjected to functional analysis using GO enrichment.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>The PacBio long reads and Illumina short reads were uploaded to the NCBI SRA database under BioProject PRJNA549758. The final chromosome-scale genome assembly was submitted to the NCBI with accession number VHIU00000000. The genome fasta and gff3 files were uploaded to Figshare.</p>
